**Bloom states + voice.** `setBloomState` (`yumi-ui.js:984`) toggles one `yumi-bloom--<state>` class on the in-panel Bloom for `listening|thinking|speaking|acting` (resting = base motion); the body FAB stays at rest. Voice-in routes both push-to-talk and hands-free through the single `VoiceInput.listen` site (`voice-input.js:24`), which handles `unsupported`/`denied`/`no-speech`/`recognition` gracefully; the mic button disables itself when `VoiceInput.isSupported()` is false (`yumi-ui.js:1133`). Voice-out (`playLine`, `integrations.js:2039`) is gated on `isVoiceOn()` (default false, `yumi-ui.js:998`) and the `opts.speak` flag set ONLY on the gated normal-chat reply (`yumi-ui.js:1248`); every TTS failure path (non-OK, decode, autoplay-blocked, over-budget) calls `onEnd` and stays silent (`integrations.js:2050/2063/2067`).

### REGRESSIONS / RISKS

**Chat fetch has no timeout and no AbortController ‚Äî the one user-facing hang path.** `sendMessage`'s primary `fetch` (`yumi-brain.js:770`) is NOT wrapped in `_yumiWithTimeout`. Evidence: `grep -c "_yumiWithTimeout(call" js/yumi-brain.js` = 8, against 12 `claude-proxy` fetch sites (`grep -n "fetch('/.netlify/functions/claude-proxy'" js/yumi-brain.js`); the 3 unwrapped are :92 (`summarizeAndRoll`), :770 (`sendMessage`, the chat path), :926 (`generateLenses`). `grep -rn "AbortController" js/` matches ONLY `import-capture.js:1054-1055` ‚Äî never yumi-brain/yumi-ui. If the proxy accepts the connection but never responds, the `.then`/`.catch`/`.finally` chain (`yumi-ui.js:1238-1257`) never settles: the typing indicator persists, `yumi_request_in_flight` stays `true`, and Send stays disabled with no recovery. Contrast: the GATE has a 12 s fail-closed timeout, so the *grading* of a reply can't hang ‚Äî only the primary reply fetch can. This is exactly the "hang-without-recovery" the audit calls out (CLAUDE.md "fail gracefully ‚Ä¶ not a generic crash").

**Orphaned user turn on proxy failure (acknowledged, unaddressed).** `sendMessage` appends the user turn to memory (`appendTurn('user', ‚Ä¶)`, `yumi-brain.js:758`) BEFORE the fetch; on any rejection the assistant turn is never appended. The in-code comment at :755-757 documents this ("the user turn persists without a matching assistant turn"; control grep `"user turn persists without a matching"` matches :756). The result: a failed send leaves a dangling user turn that subsequently appears in the transparency "Recent turns" view and in Yumi's next context, with no assistant reply. Git history shows no follow-up fix (`git log -- js/yumi-brain.js`).

### DIVERGENCE

**Panel substrate vs audit scope.** The audit brief labels this surface "(bright)", but `.yumi-panel` and `.yumi-bloom` are in the dark-ground selector (`theme.css:336-340`), so the chat panel renders on the dark study substrate at every route. The transparency content, however, is ground-sensitive via tokens: the in-panel fold inherits dark (`.yumi-panel` ‚Üí `--surface-d`), while the routed `#yumi-sees` page resolves to bright (`views.js:369` `umberGroundDark` omits `yumi-sees`). The SAME `buildTransparencyContent` output therefore renders on two different grounds depending on entry point. Both are legible (tokens adapt), but it is a visual-identity inconsistency for one shared builder.

**Dead CSS from the Umber rename (self-flagged).** `components.css:10134` explicitly notes the drift: `.yumi-panel-sight-link rules go dead (renamed) ‚Äî drift, flagged`. The JS now emits `.yumi-panel-sight` (the button, `yumi-ui.js:1042`) and `.yumi-panel-sight-back`; the old `.yumi-panel-sight-link` rules (`components.css:241-251`, 11 lines) match no element.

### COULD (see structured coulds)
Timeout+abort the chat fetch; close the orphaned-turn gap; retire dead exports/CSS; reconcile the two-ground transparency identity; add a logged-out sign-in prompt to `#yumi-sees`.

## Import & Capture + Shared Writing Surfaces

Files audited in full: `js/import-capture.js` (1421 LOC), `js/writing-canvas.js` (659), `js/spotlight.js` (457), `js/voice-input.js` (167), plus the editor entry points `openEditor`/`openJournalEditor`/`openArcEditor`/`openMarginaliaEditor`/`openArtifactEditor` in `js/views.js` and the marginalia card render path (`js/views.js:10699-10710`).

### Architecture (verified IS)

**WritingCanvas ‚Äî ONE shared core, ONE adopter.** `createWritingCanvas(mountEl, opts) -> handle` (`js/writing-canvas.js:114`) is the substrate-agnostic contenteditable writing core: live block transforms (`# / ## / - / * / 1. / [] / [x] / >`), inline `**bold**`/`*italic*` on load + via the contextual B/I control, a markdown-snapshot undo/redo stack (cap 300, `js/writing-canvas.js:539`), debounced autosave (700ms, `js/writing-canvas.js:531`), a "Saved/Saving‚Ä¶/Couldn't save" cue, and focus mode (`body.wc-focus`). The canonical stored value is markdown plain-text; `wcRenderMarkdown` (`js/writing-canvas.js:36`, top-level extracted in 2c) is the SINGLE renderer the editor, undo, setValue, and the saved marginalia card all reuse ‚Äî closing the editor/card render split. **Only `openMarginaliaEditor` (`js/views.js:10148`) adopts it.** Confirmed by grep: `createWritingCanvas` has exactly one caller (`js/views.js:10156`). The other writing surfaces are UNADOPTED and still route through the legacy raw-`<textarea>` `openEditor` (`js/views.js:2002`): `openJournalEditor` (`:2098`), `openArcEditor` (`:2143`), and `openArtifactEditor` (`:10221`). So journal, arc-create, and artifact composition get none of the markdown affordances, autosave, undo stack, or focus mode marginalia now has ‚Äî a divided writing substrate (memory's "OTHER surfaces UNADOPTED" is accurate).

**Import & Capture ‚Äî IIFE engine + FIXED overlay.** `js/import-capture.js` exposes `window.ImportCapture` (`:1407`) with `open/close/segmentDoc/matchBook/commitEntries`. The engine: `segmentDoc(rawText)` (`:129`) ‚Üí claude-proxy strict-JSON segmentation (`SEG_MODEL='claude-sonnet-4-6'`, `temperature:0`, `max_tokens:4096`); `matchBook(guess)` (`:191`) ‚Üí two-pass title-then-author resolution against the current user's deduped library (no network); `commitEntries(items)` (`:260`) ‚Üí batched write of the locked 11-field entry, de-duped on `(body|bookId)` against existing + in-batch entries, ONE `markNotebookDirty`+`saveState`+render. Mutation is gated by `ownsEntry` (`:773`) ‚Äî every flip/file/undo touches only an id in THIS import's `createdIds`. Dictation v2 (`:1082` `recordAndTranscribe`) is MediaRecorder ‚Üí gated `transcribe-proxy` (Scribe), with a real 20s `AbortController` hard timeout (`:1054-1062`) and a single-settle guard so the abort and a late response can't double-fire. The overlay mounts FIXED over the notebook (routing untouched); the trigger button is in the notebook header (`js/views.js:773-779`), guarded on `window.ImportCapture`.

**Spotlight (‚åòK).** `js/spotlight.js` builds a `role=dialog` overlay once, self-inits on DOMContentLoaded, binds a module-scoped ‚åòK/Ctrl+K (`:411`, fires regardless of focus), and wires the inert nav search pill (`:432`). Four capped groups (sub-theories/books/authors/arcs+notes, cap 5 each, `:47`). Full keyboard model (arrows wrap, Enter selects, Esc closes, `:383`) and focus restore to the trigger on close (`:360`). User text reaches the DOM via `textContent` only.

**Voice-input.** `js/voice-input.js` wraps the Web Speech API (`window.SpeechRecognition || webkitSpeechRecognition`). Per its own docstring it is the SOLE `SpeechRecognition` site, used by the Yumi talk-mode mic. **Note: the import-capture dictation path does NOT use VoiceInput** ‚Äî it uses its own `recordAndTranscribe` MediaRecorder transport (`js/import-capture.js:1082`, docstring `:997` "Replaces the Web Speech / VoiceInput dependency"). So VoiceInput is consumed only by the Yumi panel, not by Capture.

### ES3 / token conformance

All four files are ES3-clean: `const/let/arrow/class/template-literal/.catch/.finally` = 0 true violations (the lone `class` and backtick grep hits in spotlight.js:6,8 are in comments; var control 18-235 per file). One inline hex exists ‚Äî `#FFF8E7` at `js/spotlight.js:240` (idea-chip radial inner-light core, single-sourced with the constellation mark per the comment) ‚Äî a soft token-drift note (the hard CSS-token rule governs theme/components.css, not inline JS). All `innerHTML` writes are `''` or static SVG constants; no user text is ever interpolated into markup.

### Regressions / fragility (see ledger)

The load-bearing gaps: (1) **`segmentDoc` has no client-side timeout/abort** (`:141`, contrast the dictation transport's 20s `AbortController`), so a slow/hung claude-proxy strands the bulk-import "Reading your notes‚Ä¶" beat and the dictation "sorting your note‚Ä¶" beat (`:1262`) ‚Äî neither passes the `onType` escape, so neither renders the close button or "type instead" link (only the undiscoverable scrim-click survives). For dictation this is data-bearing: the transcript is committed only AFTER segmentDoc resolves, so a hang loses the just-dictated note. (2) **`flushSave` never persists an empty doc** (`js/writing-canvas.js:526`) yet sets `lastSaved=''` first (`:525`) ‚Äî emptying a marginalia note leaves a stale non-empty body in state with no way to clear it from the canvas. (3) **`destroy()` clears the pending `saveTimer` without flushing** (`js/writing-canvas.js:641`); the marginalia "Done" button (`js/views.js:10201`) relies on the click first blurring the editor ‚Üí `onBlur`‚Üí`flushSave`, which holds for mouse but is fragile for keyboard/programmatic close. (4) **No upload size guard** (`js/import-capture.js:462-469`): a large file is read whole and segmented under a 4096-token output cap, silently dropping notes past the budget ‚Äî contradicting the prompt's "omitting a note is an error." (5) Spotlight author rows route to the generic `#books` (`:134`) and note rows to `#notebook` (`:176`) ‚Äî selection lands on an unfiltered surface, no highlight/scroll to the hit.


### Named 2.0 focus areas

## Sub-theory building flow ‚Äî end-to-end audit

The sub-theory is Praxis's central intellectual artifact: the place where gathered reading becomes an argued, cited claim. This section traces the full lifecycle ‚Äî **create ‚Üí compose ‚Üí cite-weave ‚Üí register ‚Üí maturity ‚Üí Yumi-in-margin** ‚Äî against the actual code, then measures it against an Apple/Claude-grade compose experience.

### Flow map (verified, file:line)

**1. Create ‚Äî four entry points, all funneling through one constructor.**
- Arc page `+ Sub-theory` button ‚Üí `location.hash = 'arc/<id>/new-subtheory'` (`js/views.js:9603`), routed at `js/views.js:482` which mints an **empty** draft via `createSubTheory(parts[1], {})` and `location.replace`s to `#subtheory/<id>` (history-safe so Back doesn't re-mint).
- Constellation control-bar `+ Sub-theory` (web view; the header button is suppressed in web to avoid duplication, `js/views.js:9598`).
- Notebook **gather ‚Üí Create** bridge: `notebookCreateSubTheory()` (`js/views.js:1319`) reuses `createSubTheory(arcId, {header:name})` then loops `addEvidenceToSubTheory(... kind:'entry', quote:body)` over the gathered ids, then routes to the new page (`js/views.js:1328-1339`). Arc defaults to the intersection of gathered notes' `arcIds` (`notebookSharedArc`, `js/views.js:1264`) else a user pick via `openGatherArcPicker` (`js/views.js:1300`).
- Yumi NAME-accept: `nameSubTheoryFromThread()` (`js/views.js:1848`) seeds `bodyPublic` with the accepted one-line read and attaches the thread notes as evidence.
- Constructor `createSubTheory(arcId, fields)` (`js/state.js:1730`) validates the arc exists, stamps `userId`, initializes `status:'draft'`, `publishedAt:null`, empty `evidence`/`attachedMarginalia`/`linkedSubTheories`/`citationPins`, then `markSubTheoriesDirty()` + `saveState()`.

**2. Compose ‚Äî two registers, plain textareas.** `renderSubTheoryPage(id)` (`js/views.js:7467`, a 1070-line function ‚Äî `awk 'NR>=7467 && NR<=8536' | wc -l` = 1070) builds: eyebrow ‚Üí head (mark chip + title input + Delete) ‚Üí maturity band ‚Üí a segmented **Public | Intellectual** register toggle (`js/views.js:7575-7690`) ‚Üí a **Write | Preview** toggle (`js/views.js:7648`) ‚Üí a **Published** read-only toggle (`js/views.js:7720`) ‚Üí the `.manuscript` with two `<textarea>` bodies (`publicBody`/`intelBody`, `js/views.js:7582-7596`). Both registers persist on **blur only** (`updateSubTheory(id, {...})` at `js/views.js:7548,7587,7595`); `input` is wired solely to cite-preview refresh and `*`-autocomplete (`js/views.js:8087-8090`). The textareas are `min-height:300px; resize:vertical` (`assets/components.css:10047`) ‚Äî **no autogrow** (the only `scrollHeight` autogrow in views.js is the notebook writeline at `js/views.js:1541`).

**3. Cite-weave ‚Äî asterisk convention + a parallel preview pane.** The author wraps a source title in `*asterisks*`; `parseCitations(bodyText, evidenceTitles)` (`js/views.js:7211`) walks the text and, for each `*phrase*`, matches against attached-evidence titles by **bidirectional substring** (`lc.indexOf(tl) !== -1 || tl.indexOf(lc) !== -1`, `js/views.js:7249`). Matches render as `.subtheory-cite` underline-dot spans in a read-only preview pane (`renderCitationPreview`, `js/views.js:8030`); >1 candidate ‚Üí `.subtheory-cite-ambiguous` with a right-click/long-press chooser whose choice persists to `citationPins` (`js/views.js:7895-7950`, `state.js:656`). A `*`-keystroke opens an autocomplete of attached titles (`js/views.js:7952-8023`). The evidence rail's per-item **Cite** button inserts `*Title*` at the last-focused caret (`insertCitationAtCursor`, `js/views.js:7608`). Citation match-titles come only from books / external sources / *titled* entries ‚Äî untitled marginalia/journal contribute nothing (`citationMatchTitle`, `js/views.js:7759`).

**4. Evidence rail (the "gather" half of the page).** `.st-gutter` (`js/views.js:8097`) lists **Attached** evidence (`refreshAttached`, `js/views.js:8264`) and a disclosure-collapsed picker of **From this arc** books + non-private entries (`js/views.js:8363-8410`) plus an **Add external source** form requiring a title (`js/views.js:8426-8485`). Attaching routes through `addEvidence` (`state.js:1991`) / `addEvidenceToSubTheory` (`state.js:2064`, dedupes via `isEvidenceAttached`). Private/missing journal entries are tagged "private ‚Äî excluded when published" in the rail (`js/views.js:8225-8233`). On mobile (`max-width:759px`) the rail becomes a bottom sheet with backdrop + Escape (`js/views.js:8116-8137`, `assets/components.css:10062`).

**5. Maturity ‚Äî cosmetic only.** `_stComputeMaturity(sub)` (`js/views.js:8754`) = `(bodyPublic.len + bodyIntellectual.len + 80¬∑evidenceCount) / 1500`, clamped 0‚Äì1, banded nascent/developing/established for a label + glow opacity (`js/views.js:7556-7565`) and a constellation hint (`js/views.js:8692`). It gates **nothing**.

**6. Register / publish ‚Äî UNIMPLEMENTED.** This is the structural gap. `status` is only ever written to `'draft'` (`state.js:661`; the migrate/ensure default) and `publishedAt` is never assigned anywhere (`grep "\.status = 'published'"` ‚Üí 0 hits in any sub-theory path; the only views.js `status` writes are book read-status). The **"Published" toggle does not publish** ‚Äî it swaps in `renderSubTheoryReadOnly(rec, 'published')` (`js/views.js:7737`), a transient read-only preview keyed by a `mode` *argument*, never by the record's `status`. There is no "publish this sub-theory," no public/private surfacing of finished theories, no audience. The read-only render itself is solid (numbered superscript citations in first-appearance order, private-evidence exclusion, see-also links; `js/views.js:7285-7464`) but it is reachable only as a self-preview.

**7. Yumi-in-margin ‚Äî ABSENT on this surface.** Despite "Yumi-in-margin" being the named terminal step, `renderSubTheoryPage` has **zero** Yumi hooks. `considerArcVoice` lives on the arc detail page (`js/views.js:9363,9379`); `considerMove` (COMPLICATE) lives in the notebook (`js/views.js:1807`); the notebook's working leaf even renders a *resting* "Yumi complicates" placeholder (`js/views.js:1189-1208`). The sub-theory writing page ‚Äî the one place an author argues a claim from evidence ‚Äî gets no draw-out, no complicate, no margin presence at all.

### Where it falls short of Apple/Claude-grade compose

- **Two competing writing substrates.** The shared `WritingCanvas` (live-markdown, Apple-Notes-in-Umber; shipped v3.150) is adopted in the marginalia editor (`js/views.js:10137-10156`) but **not** here ‚Äî the sub-theory page is the older split-pane "Write | Preview" model with no inline rendering, no markdown (only `*cite*` resolution), and a separate preview pane the author must toggle to. A best-in-class composer renders inline as you type.
- **Blur-only saves with no input-level autosave.** Prose persists only on `blur` (`js/views.js:7587,7595`); a hash navigation triggers `renderRoute`‚Üí`host.innerHTML=''` (`js/views.js:609`) with no `beforeunload` and no pre-route `activeElement.blur()` flush (both greps empty). This is a fragility class for in-flight text (see RLV).
- **No keyboard affordances.** No `metaKey`/`ctrlKey` handlers on the page (grep empty) ‚Äî no ‚åòB/‚åòI, no ‚åò‚Üµ to cite, no ‚åòS. Citation insertion is mouse-first.
- **Substring citation matching over-matches.** Bidirectional `indexOf` (`js/views.js:7249`) means a one-word title ("Discipline") matches any `*phrase*` containing it, or `*the*` matches every title containing "the" ‚Äî quietly producing false ambiguity.
- **Fixed-height manuscript.** No autogrow; long prose forces an inner scroll or manual drag-resize.

### Friction points & dead ends (verified)
- Creating from the arc page mints an **empty untitled draft immediately** (`js/views.js:483`), even on an accidental click ‚Äî a stray draft with no undo prompt (Delete is the only exit).
- The author has **no path to "finish/publish"** a sub-theory; the artifact has no destination beyond the writing page.
- Maturity is presented as a meaningful signal but is purely length¬∑evidence arithmetic with no qualitative input.

This surface is feature-rich on the *gather-and-cite* half and structurally incomplete on the *register-and-ship* half, with the marquee "Yumi-in-margin" affordance entirely missing.

## Arcs ‚Äî list, constellation/field, and interior

The Arcs experience spans three surfaces wired through `renderRoute` (js/views.js:386, all under `activeRoute='arcs'`): the **list/teaching page** `renderArcsPage` (#arcs, js/views.js:2244), the **interior** `renderArcDetail` (#arc/<id>, js/views.js:9477) which itself toggles between a **List** member-stream and a **Web** sub-theory constellation, and the standalone `#arc/<id>/new-subtheory` mint route. The live constellation is drawn by `renderSubTheoryConstellation` (js/arc-constellation.js:1223) with interaction layers `_stConstellationAttachInteractions` (js/views.js:8832) + `attachSubTheoryDrag` (js/arc-constellation.js:1354).

### How connections read

The interior's information scent is strong on desktop-hover and weak everywhere else. Sub-theory marks are 16 frozen identity shapes orbiting an italic-serif question (`_stRenderShapes` js/arc-constellation.js:898; `_stRenderQuestion` :840); a hover **card** in `attachSubTheoryDrag` surfaces header + a maturity word (`maturityRead`: Nascent/Forming/Developing/Mature, :1492) + gathered count (:1502). A bottom legend teaches the grammar ‚Äî resonance/faint/gathered/incorporated/book (`_stRenderLegend` :1117). Attached books render as anonymous neutral squares (`_stRenderBooks` :1176) and resonance threads as amber gradient lines (`_stRenderEdges` :1080). The empty state is a graceful italic prompt, "Begin a sub-theory to map this question." (`_stRenderEmpty` :859).

The weakness: **identity is hover-or-tap-only, and the gates exclude touch and keyboard.** The sub-theory hover card binds only when `!isTouch` (js/arc-constellation.js:1672); the mark/Yumi tooltips bind only when `!isTouch` (js/views.js:9005). Book squares get a click handler (js/views.js:8996) but **no hover tooltip and no keyboard focus** ‚Äî the focusable loop covers shapes + marks only (js/views.js:9013-9019), so the books-in-arc carry no `tabindex`/`role`/`aria-label` and no readable label at all in the Web view. A keyboard user cannot open a book from the field; a touch user sees only anonymous shapes and squares that, on tap, immediately navigate away ‚Äî no preview is possible. The List view and the rail (`buildArcFieldRail` js/views.js:9423) do label books, so this is a Web-view-specific scent/access gap, not total loss.

### Navigation between the three views

The cross-surface story is incoherent for a newcomer. Arcs live as cards on **#arcs** (the only "Your arcs" grid, js/views.js:2318) and as rows on **#account** (`_accountArcRow` :11724). The Notebook has **no** arc list ‚Äî `renderArcRow` (:10925), which built the old `notebook-arc-row`, is dead (referenced only in a comment at :11708). Yet every interior exit routes to **#notebook**: the not-found fallbacks (js/views.js:9504, 9517), the user-arc delete redirect (`location.hash='#notebook'` :10100, justified by a comment claiming Notebook is "where their other arcs live" ‚Äî false), and the stale-note "Back to Notebook" link (:10112). So a user who reaches an arc from #arcs and deletes it is dropped onto a surface that contains zero arcs. (The create path is fine: `openArcEditor` calls `renderRoute()` not `renderNotebook()` on save/cancel (js/views.js:2155,2158) ‚Äî the long comment at :2176 claiming it lands on the Notebook is stale.)

### Computed counts

The list-card meta line (`_arcCardMetaText` js/views.js:2215 over `_arcCardCounts` :2185) and the interior sub-meta (js/views.js:9562-9585) are honest display-only aggregations: books from `arc.bookIds`, sub-theories by scanning `state.subTheories` for matching `arcId`, marginalia from `arc.entryIds` filtered to `register==='marginalia'`. They render real data and pluralize correctly. One redundancy: `_arcCardCounts` and the interior sub-meta each independently re-walk `state.subTheories` (O(N) per arc) rather than sharing a helper.

### Structural divergence from the bar (dead weight)

Arc rendering carries a large dead substrate from the pre-sub-theory "book constellation" era, none of it reachable:
- **`renderArcConstellation` + its 9 private helpers** (js/arc-constellation.js:59-467, 409 LOC): never called, never exported (only `renderSubTheoryConstellation`/`attachSubTheoryDrag` are exported, :1778-1779).
- **The old book-interaction cluster** in views.js (`_arcConstellationAttachInteractions` :9033 + `_arcAttachClickHandlers`/`_arcAttachTooltipHandlers`/`_arcAttachKeyboardHandlers`/`_arcBindBookClick`/`_arcBindMarginaliaClick`/`_arcBuildBookIndex`/`_arcFindThread`/`_arcEngagementLabel`, ~290 LOC, 9033-9322): `_arcConstellationAttachInteractions` is referenced only in a comment (:8822). `_arcMakeFocusable` (:9324) is the one live member of this block (used by the sub-theory layer).
- **`_arcDetailBuildConstellationData`** (js/views.js:8615): the old books-adapter, referenced only in comments (:8648, :9024).
- **`_stTreatment`/`_stRenderMarks`/`_stSilhouette`** (arc-constellation.js): each defined once, zero call sites ‚Äî the source comment at :895-897 admits they "remain as dead code (removal is a later cleanup)."

### CSS: two competing card systems + a non-matching mobile rule

There are two overlapping `.arc-card` rule families. The pre-Umber block (assets/components.css:1610-1808) sets `.arc-card { padding:20px; background:var(--surface-2); border:1px solid var(--ink-4) }` plus now-dead descendants `.arc-card-text` (:1626), `.arc-card-description` (:1640), `.arc-card-covers`/`.arc-card-cover`/`.arc-card-cover-placeholder` (:1730-1772) ‚Äî none of those classes are emitted by JS anymore (canon ¬ß4-G dropped the 5 cover thumbnails; JS emits `.arc-card-body`/`.arc-card-desc`/`.arc-card-thumb`). The Umber block (:1822-1833, scoped `.arcs .arc-card`) is the live design: full-bleed `.arc-card-thumb` (height:140px, edge-to-edge `border-bottom`) with inner padding only on body/meta. Because `.arcs .arc-card` never resets padding, the early `.arc-card { padding:20px }` (0,1,0) still applies, insetting the "full-bleed" banner by 20px [requires live verification of the visual].

Worse, the **mobile 1-up collapse never fires**: the rule at assets/components.css:5730-5733 (inside `@media (max-width:759px)`) targets class selectors `.arcs-yours, .arcs-examples`, but `renderArcsPage` emits these as **ids** on class-`arcs-grid` elements (`yoursSec.className='arcs-grid'; yoursSec.id='arcs-yours'`, js/views.js:2319-2320; same for examples :2416-2417). No `#arcs-yours`/`#arcs-examples` selector exists. With `.arcs-grid { grid-template-columns:repeat(3,1fr) }` (:1821) ungarded, the Arcs grids stay **3-up on phones**, violating canon ¬ß4-F (1-up mobile). The interior `.arcfield-stage` correctly collapses (`grid-template-columns:1fr` at :10126), so this is a list-page-only regression. `.arc-card-meta` is also defined twice with divergent color tokens (`--ink-3` at :1684 vs `--gold` at :1829; the `.arcs`-scoped gold wins).

### Token/contrast notes

The constellation legend (`_stRenderLegend`) fills labels with `var(--ink-2)` (js/arc-constellation.js:1129) which remaps to `--muted` #c2a87f on the dark `.arcfield` ground ‚Äî small italic 10.5-11px text on the dark stage; the foundation's sub-AA inventory makes this a likely fine-print contrast risk [requires live verification]. The arc-card-meta on the list page uses `--gold` #a8741a on `--surface` ‚Äî corroborated as borderline by the foundation contrast pass.

## How the user views their own notes & marginalia (data-display)

This audit covers the *reading* side of the notebook: how a captured note, marginalia entry, or journal/question is shown back to the reader on the Notebook spread (`renderNotebook` js/views.js:734), on Book detail (`renderBookDetail` filtered list js/views.js:6721-6755), on the Arc detail page (`renderNotebookEntry` js/views.js:9997), in the Account "reader-portrait" (`renderAccountPage` js/views.js:13167 + `buildReaderModelSection` js/views.js:11935), and in the two transparency surfaces (`openTransparencyView` js/views.js:11105 / `renderWhatYumiSeesPage` js/views.js:11303, both via `buildTransparencyContent` js/views.js:11132). The single shared card renderer is `renderNotebookEntry` (js/views.js:10637).

### The core display path is sound but has one capture/display split and one silent clip

`renderNotebookEntry` builds a clean card: register pill, timestamp, a visibility dot, an optional "from <book>" source line for marginalia, the body, inline photos, and an actions row. It is reused verbatim across the notebook spread, book detail, and arc detail (js/views.js:1040, 6752, 9997) ‚Äî good single-source discipline.

Two divergences undercut "re-read your own thinking," however:

- **Markdown renders for marginalia only.** The body is rendered through the editor's own renderer `wcRenderMarkdown` (writing-canvas.js:36) **only when `register === 'marginalia'`** (js/views.js:10705-10710). Journal and question entries fall to `bodyEl.textContent = entry.body`. But the notebook composer (`buildNotebookWriteline` js/views.js:1535) is a plain `<textarea>` for *all three* registers, and the Talk-to-Yumi / import paths capture markdown-bearing prose into any register. So a journal or question note containing `# heading`, `- bullets`, or `**bold**` is shown back to its author as raw asterisks and hashes ‚Äî the writing the reader sees does not match the writing they composed. Compounding this, the *upright* markdown render (`.notebook-entry-body-md`, components.css:10615) and the *italic 20px Cormorant* plain render (`.notebook-entry-body`, components.css:4179-4187) are visually different substrates, so two marginalia notes can look like different kinds of object purely based on which capture surface created them (book-detail's `openMarginaliaEditor` js/views.js:10156 uses the live-render WritingCanvas; the notebook writeline does not).

- **Marginalia is silently clipped with no escape.** `.notebook-entry-body-md { max-height:15em; overflow:hidden; }` (components.css:10615) hard-clips rendered marginalia at ~15em with no fade, no "read more," and no per-entry detail route. A grep for any expand affordance over entries returns nothing (`read more|show more|expand|truncat` ‚Üí no entry-level hit; the only `account-expand-*` matches are the unrelated account arc rows). There is **no `#entry/` route** (`grep "#entry/|renderEntryDetail|renderNoteDetail"` ‚Üí no matches) and the card carries no whole-card click handler. The plain `.notebook-entry-body` path is *not* clipped, so on book detail a long marginalia note is cut off while an equally long journal note beside it is shown in full ‚Äî an inconsistent and unrecoverable truncation. The reader literally cannot finish reading their own long marginalia from the UI.

### Body legibility: full-italic serif at 20px for long-form prose

`.notebook-entry-body` sets the entire note in `font-family:var(--font-serif); font-style:italic; font-size:20px` (components.css:4179-4187). Italic is an emphasis style; setting a whole multi-sentence note in italic serif is a recognised long-form-readability cost, and it is the default for every journal and question entry and for any marginalia that bypasses the markdown renderer. The design canon reserves italic-serif for *titles/italics*, not body (CLAUDE.md ¬ß1 fonts). The mono timestamp uses `--ink-4` (components.css:4135), which on the bright notebook/book-detail ground resolves to `--meta #9a7e4e` ‚Äî a foundation-measured 3.41-3.56 contrast, below WCAG AA for this small meta text.

### Re-finding your own writing is effectively unsupported

- **No search, filter, or sort over notes.** `grep "notebook.*search|nb-search|notebook-filter|notebook-sort|sortEntries"` ‚Üí no matches. The only organisation is the fixed tab model (Inbox / Journal / one-per-book, `buildNotebookTabModel` js/views.js:895) and a single createdAt-desc sort (js/views.js:819). There is no way to find a note by text, by register, by date, or by privacy from within the notebook.
- **Spotlight finds notes but cannot navigate to them.** `‚åòK` does match `en.body` (spotlight.js:168) and labels marginalia/note results ‚Äî but every note result routes to the bare `#notebook` (spotlight.js:176), with no entry id, no tab selection, and no scroll-into-view. Selecting a found note drops the reader on whatever tab was last active, with the target note neither selected nor scrolled to (and possibly under a different tab). Search surfaces the note's existence but does not return the reader to it.
- **The reader-portrait shows counts, never the writing.** The entire Account "what your reading reveals" cluster ‚Äî RETURNS (`_portraitReturnsData` js/views.js:12945, "Book X ‚Äî your densest margins ¬∑ 7 notes"), FIELD/GALAXY (`_portraitAxisData` js/views.js:12471), THREADS, JOURNEY (`_portraitJourneyData` js/views.js:13105), and the EMBLEM capstone (js/views.js:13932) ‚Äî aggregates marginalia into counts, stars, and shapes. It tells the reader *how much* and *where* they wrote but never surfaces a single line of *what* they wrote, and offers no link from a count back to the underlying notes. The richest "view your thinking" surface in the app contains none of the thinking.

### The Account page renders the reader-model threads ‚Äî and its consent toggle ‚Äî twice

On `#account` the reader's named threads appear in two separate blocks that both read `getReaderModel(uid).threads`: the portrait "threads" card (`renderPortraitThreads` js/views.js:13831-13868, rows at :13847) and `buildReaderModelSection`'s "Recurring themes" list (js/views.js:12304-12317, via `buildThreadItem` :11989). Each block also renders its **own** toggle for the **same** `yumiReaderModel` flag ‚Äî `setProfile(uid,{yumiReaderModel:...})` is written from two sites on one page (js/views.js:13862 and js/views.js:11954; confirmed by grep). The reader sees their themes listed twice and two switches that silently mean the same thing ‚Äî a duplication-of-truth on a single scroll that the v3.112 lesson (CLAUDE.md "rendered count must equal stored count") warns against.

### The "inert composition-section pop-ups"

The display-heavy inline panels Preston named are the picker/transparency mounts that open *inside* the composing surfaces rather than as real overlays. They are functional but read as inert blocks: `openTransparencyView` (js/views.js:11105) injects the full "What Yumi sees" panel into `#notebook-transparency-host` *above* the spread (it pushes the whole notebook down rather than overlaying); `openEntryArcPicker` / `openEntrySendToSubTheory` / `openFileToBookPicker` (js/views.js:10383, 10612, 1961) and the gather arc picker (`openGatherArcPicker` js/views.js:1300) lazily append a `.arc-picker-panel` / `.subtheory-picker-panel` into a per-card host with no backdrop, no focus trap, and no scroll-into-view, so on a long card the panel can open below the fold. The right-leaf composer also carries two genuinely *inert* placeholder blocks: the reserved Yumi COMPLICATE slot (js/views.js:1189-1208, hardcoded "Once Yumi's reading along, she'll open a question here") and the name-block eyebrow ‚Äî static chrome that occupies prime composing real estate while doing nothing. The transparency panel itself (`buildTransparencyContent`) renders bodies that `assembleContextData` already truncated to 200 chars and shows only the 3 most-recent visible entries (js/views.js:11221-11236), so even this "everything Yumi sees" surface cannot be used to re-read a note in full.

### What works well (for balance)

Single-source rendering across three surfaces; `notebookEntryMatchesTab` (js/views.js:877) guarantees a tab's count and its rendered entries cannot disagree; the reader-model panel is fully namespaced under `.account-readermodel` (components.css:9700+) with editable threads, an editable arc-prose block, per-item delete, and a "Forget everything" control that wipes data even when consent is off (js/views.js:12417-12428) ‚Äî the correctability covenant is genuinely honoured. The portrait sections are each wrapped in `try/catch` (js/views.js:13312, 13895, 13923) so one failing section degrades to "absent" rather than blanking the page (the v3.143 fix).

## Composing surfaces & the WritingCanvas seam

### Summary

Praxis ships a purpose-built shared composing core, `createWritingCanvas` (`js/writing-canvas.js`), with a clean handle-only contract (getValue/setValue/insertAtCaret/getSelection/onSelectionChange/focus/destroy), a contenteditable substrate, live markdown block-rendering, an inline B/I/H/‚Ä¢/1./‚òê/‚ùù toolbar, debounced autosave with a save cue, a markdown-snapshot undo/redo stack, and a focus-mode that recedes the nav. It is **adopted at exactly one of the eight-plus places a user writes prose**: the book-detail marginalia editor (`openMarginaliaEditor`, `js/views.js:10156`). Every other composing surface is a divergent raw `<textarea>`. The seam is real and the core is sound; the 2.0 work is adoption, not invention.

Verified: `createWritingCanvas(` is called once (`js/views.js:10156`); `wcRenderMarkdown(` is called once for display (`js/views.js:10707`, marginalia cards only); there are 11 raw `createElement('textarea')` sites in `views.js` plus 2 in `import-capture.js`.

### Inventory of every writing surface

| Surface | Entry point | Substrate | Autogrow | Live markdown render | Toolbar | Placeholder |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Marginalia editor** (book detail) | `openMarginaliaEditor` `views.js:10148` | **WritingCanvas** (contenteditable) | grows (div, `min-height:220px` `components.css:10542`) | **yes** (live block transforms) | **yes** (`wc-fmt`) | "Write in the margin‚Ä¶" |
| **Notebook writeline** (marginalia/journal/question) | `buildNotebookWriteline` `views.js:1528` | raw `<textarea.nb-ce>` | **yes, JS** (`autogrowWriteline` `views.js:1539`, `resize:none` `components.css:9873`) | **no** | **no** | "Write a note‚Ä¶" |
| **Journal entry editor** | `openJournalEditor`‚Üí`openEditor` `views.js:2098/2028` | raw `<textarea.notebook-editor-body rows=8>` | **no** | **no** | **no** | (none on body) |
| **Arc create editor** | `openArcEditor`‚Üí`openEditor` `views.js:2143/2028` | raw `<textarea>` (`min-height:72px;height:72px` `components.css:1841`) | **no** | **no** | **no** | "What question or thread runs through it?" |
| **Artifact editor** | `openArtifactEditor`‚Üí`openEditor` `views.js:10221/2028` | raw `<textarea rows=8>` | **no** | **no** | **no** | (none) |
| **Sub-theory PUBLIC register** | `renderSubTheory‚Ä¶` `views.js:7582` | raw `<textarea.subtheory-register-body min-height:300px resize:vertical>` `components.css:10047` | **no** | **no** (editor); display via `parseCitations`, italic-only | **no** | "Write the public register‚Ä¶" |
| **Sub-theory INTELLECTUAL register** | `views.js:7590` | same | **no** | **no** | **no** | "Write the intellectual register‚Ä¶" |
| **Evidence inline attach** (quote+annotation) | `buildInlineEvidenceEditor` `views.js:8289/8293` | raw `<textarea rows=2>` √ó2 | **no** | **no** | **no** | "Quote/Annotation (optional)" |
| **Evidence external-source attach** | `views.js:8437/8441` | raw `<textarea rows=2>` √ó2 | **no** | **no** | **no** | same |
| **Reader-model thread edit** | `startEdit` `views.js:12033` | raw `<textarea.rm-edit-input resize:vertical min-height:54px>` `components.css:9745` | **no** | **no** | **no** | (none) |
| **Reader arc-profile** | `views.js:12366` | raw `<textarea.rm-arc-input>` | **no** | **no** | **no** | "Describe the arc‚Ä¶" |
| **Import paste / dictation fallback** | `import-capture.js:447,1155` | raw `<textarea.ic-textarea>` | **no** | **no** | **no** | "Paste notes here‚Ä¶" |

Bulk-add (`openBulkAddEditor` `views.js:4359`, "One ISBN or title per line") is structured-data entry, not prose, and is correctly excluded from the prose-core target.

### Core inconsistencies (the 2.0 unification gap)

1. **The same register is composed two completely different ways.** A *marginalia* note authored on the book-detail page gets the WritingCanvas (live markdown, toolbar, focus mode); the *same* marginalia register authored in the notebook writeline (`buildNotebookWriteline`, default register marginalia, `views.js:1546`) gets a bare textarea with no markdown affordance and no toolbar ‚Äî yet its saved card is rendered with `wcRenderMarkdown` (`views.js:10705-10707`). So markdown typed in the writeline silently appears formatted only after save, with no in-editor preview, while markdown typed in the editor previews live. Two doors to one register, two experiences.

2. **Growth behavior is inconsistent across surfaces.** Only two surfaces grow with content: the WritingCanvas (a contenteditable div) and the notebook writeline (JS `autogrowWriteline`, `views.js:1539-1543`). Every other textarea has a fixed `rows` (journal/artifact `rows=8`, evidence `rows=2`) or a fixed/`resize:vertical` CSS height (arc-create `height:72px` `components.css:1841`; sub-theory `min-height:300px` `components.css:10047`; reader-model `min-height:54px`). The sub-theory register ‚Äî the platform's *primary long-form theory-writing surface* ‚Äî does not grow; the author must hand-drag the resize handle as the manuscript lengthens.

3. **Editor/display render split persists on sub-theories.** Sub-theory bodies store markdown but are displayed by `parseCitations` (`views.js:7211`), which only understands `*italic*`/citation tokens and **explicitly leaves `**bold**` as literal asterisks** (`views.js:7236-7240`); it has no heading/list/blockquote/checkbox support. This is precisely the editor/card split the WritingCanvas's shared `wcRenderMarkdown` was extracted to close (`writing-canvas.js:29-35`) ‚Äî closed for marginalia, still open for sub-theories and for journal/question/artifact cards (which display via plain `textContent`, `views.js:10709`).

4. **Toolbar, placeholder, and focus-mode are WritingCanvas-only.** The inline format control, the "Saved/Saving‚Ä¶/Couldn't save" cue, undo/redo, and the nav-receding focus mode exist on no other surface. Placeholders are ad hoc (some surfaces have none ‚Äî journal body, artifact body, reader-model edit).

### Reliability findings on the core itself

- **`destroy()` discards an unflushed autosave (`writing-canvas.js:631-646`).** It cancels the pending `saveTimer` (`:641`) without calling `flushSave()` first. The marginalia "Done" handler calls `canvas.destroy()` then re-renders (`views.js:10201-10204`). In the normal Done path a blur fires `onBlur`‚Üí`flushSave` first (`:583`), so the keystroke is saved; but `destroy` has no flush of its own as a safety net, and there is no `destroy` call on route-away ‚Äî navigating off `#book/<id>` while the canvas is focused detaches the host via re-render without `destroy`, relying entirely on a blur firing before detachment [requires live verification].
- **`wc-focus` body class can leak the dimmed nav.** `setFocusMode` toggles `document.body.classList` `wc-focus` (`writing-canvas.js:565-568`), which dims the app nav to `opacity:.26` (`components.css:10606`). It is removed only on blur or destroy; a route change that detaches the canvas without firing blur leaves the global nav dimmed [requires live verification].
- **Dangling contract reference.** The file header cites `design/writing-core-contract.md S2` as the substrate-agnostic interface spec (`writing-canvas.js:6`), but that file does not exist in the repo (`git ls-files` shows only `js/writing-canvas.js`). The contract the seam is built against is unversioned.

### What is solid

The core is ES3-clean (0 const/let/class/arrow/template-literal/`.catch`/`.finally`; 198 var/function occurrences as control), loads before `views.js` (`index.html:52` before `:53`) and is precached (`sw.js:29`). The markdown‚ÜîDOM round-trip is designed for idempotence, the extraction of `wcRenderMarkdown` to a pure top-level function correctly de-duplicates editor and card render for marginalia, and the handle contract is the right shape for adopting the remaining surfaces. The unification target is well-formed.

## Lineage / Value-Load Data-Model Readiness

This section maps the data substrate a future "value-load" / "lineage" feature would build on ‚Äî the declared-values store, book classification, and the arc‚Üísub-theory‚Üíevidence graph ‚Äî separating what is wired today (IS) from what such a feature would need to add (COULD). It is primarily a readiness map; the ledger carries only gaps that are real bugs today.

### 1. Declared values (`profile.values`) ‚Äî stored and round-tripped, but NOT a lineage substrate

The reader's declared values ("the stones") are a first-class, durable field, but they are an isolated string list with no edges to anything else.

- **Storage shape.** `profile.values` is an array of trimmed, non-empty strings, seeded `[]` in `ensureUser` (`js/state.js:1025`, `:1050`) with an additive backfill guard (`js/state.js:1090-1093`). `setProfile` sanitizes on write ‚Äî trims, drops empties, only an explicit array writes (`js/state.js:1188-1195`). Migrate stamps the field at 1.25.x (`js/state.js:2913-2924`).
- **Cross-device durability is sound.** The field is symmetric across the Firestore merge: written by `saveProfileToFirestore` and read back at `js/integrations.js:376` (`values: (rd.values instanceof Array) ? rd.values : []`) and `:767`, so it does not suffer the "sign-in bypasses migrate() ‚Üí second device wipes it" gotcha that the inline comment there calls out.
- **DECLARED, never inferred.** Yumi has no write path into `values` (comment `js/state.js:1087-1092`); the only writer is the account-page editor `accountValuesPersist` ‚Üí `setProfile(uid, { values: accountValuesCollect() })` (`js/views.js:13345-13350`), where each stone is a free-text `data-value` (`js/views.js:13351-13365`).
- **They feed exactly one consumer: the portrait emblem.** `_portraitEmblem` reads `profile.values` to draw the central "gems" and to drive the "what it's made of" breakdown (`js/views.js:13008-13009`, `:13076-13079`), alongside live-derived counts for lenses (userThemes), traditions (book.tradition), and marginalia. This is the only place values are read into anything.
- **Values are STRICTLY ABSENT from Yumi's context.** This is the single most important readiness fact: `gatherReaderModel()` ‚Äî the consent-gated gatherer that injects reader context into all five moves + arc-voice ‚Äî reads `readerModel.threads` and `readerModel.profile.summary` only; it never touches `profile.values` (`js/yumi-brain.js:1134-1161`; grep for "values" in `js/yumi-brain.js` returns 0). `assembleContextData()`, the single Yumi-context source, likewise has no `values` slot (`js/yumi-brain.js:178-341`). So the values a reader explicitly declares as what they read toward never reach the AI that is supposed to read along ‚Äî a value-load feature's most natural hook (steer Yumi's angle by declared values) has no current wiring.

### 2. Book classification ‚Äî `category` (built/live) and `tradition` (built/live) are two parallel, unrelated axes

Two independent classification fields exist on every book record; a lineage feature would likely want to relate value ‚Üí tradition/category, but no such mapping exists.

- **`book.category` (the 17-category shelf taxonomy) is fully built and live ‚Äî NOT a Stage-2 placeholder.** The focus-area hint that Stage 2 is "unbuilt" is stale. `classifyBookLocal` resolves cached ‚Üí BISAC-keyword ‚Üí null (`js/state.js:600-617`); the LLM batch fallback `classifyBooksViaLLM` (`js/integrations.js:1846`) is wired into `renderShelf`'s Categories grouping with a generation guard, watchdog timeout, single batched persist, and re-render (`js/views.js:3138-3194`). Results cache to `book.category` and persist via `markBooksDirty()` + `saveState()` (`js/views.js:3183-3187`).
- **`volumeInfo.categories` is now CAPTURED, not discarded.** `volumeToBook` stores `rawCategories: (vi && vi.categories instanceof Array) ? vi.categories : []` (`js/integrations.js:1740`); the memory note that it is "discarded" is stale. These raw BISAC strings are the deterministic classifier's input (`js/state.js:608-613`).
- **`book.tradition` is a SECOND, genre-derived axis** (9 traditions + `unassigned`), derived via `THEME_TO_TRADITION` (`js/state.js:300-358`), with a user `traditionOverride` (`js/state.js:394-396`). The portrait reads `traditionOverride || tradition` (`js/views.js:13019`).
- **Both ride the `ensureBookFields` chokepoint** (`js/state.js:387-414`), which is honored by the Firestore merge (`ensureBookFieldsAll` at `js/integrations.js:601`), so `category` / `rawCategories` / `tradition` survive cross-device sync ‚Äî the cleanest-durability part of the lineage substrate.
- **Gap for lineage:** `category` and `tradition` are unrelated maps; neither relates to `profile.values`. There is no edge from a declared value to the books/traditions/categories that express it ‚Äî a value-load feature would have to build that relation from scratch.

### 3. The arc ‚Üí sub-theory ‚Üí evidence graph ‚Äî a real lineage substrate, forward-only

This is the strongest existing foundation for lineage. The edges exist and are traversed widely, but only in the forward direction.

- **Arc membership** carries per-membership timestamps: `arc.bookIds` / `arc.entryIds` are arrays of `{id, addedAt}` (`js/state.js:72-84`, written at `js/state.js:1616`, `:1641`), and entries hold a denormalized back-reference `entry.arcIds` (plain strings, maintained bidirectionally in `addEntryToArc` `js/state.js:1631-1664` and cleaned in `deleteArc`/`deleteEntry`). Traversed at 104 sites in views.js (`grep -n "\.bookIds\b\|\.entryIds\b" js/views.js | wc -l` = 104).
- **Evidence is the citation edge.** `addEvidence` (`js/state.js:1991-2032`) builds `{id, kind:'book'|'entry'|'external', refId, external, quote, annotation, addedAt}`. For `book`/`entry`, `refId` is the foreign key into `state.books` / `state.notebookEntries`; for `external` it self-generates a stable id with a `{title, author}` payload. This forward edge (sub-theory ‚Üí cited source, with the supporting quote) is exactly a lineage edge and is resolved in render at `js/views.js:7302-7340`, `:8167-8226`.
- **Sub-theory‚Üîsub-theory resonance** edges live in `linkedSubTheories` (symmetric, cascade-cleaned in `deleteSubTheory` `js/state.js:1805-1819`); `attachedMarginalia` is a third edge type (`js/state.js:645-648`). 27 usages across state/views.
- **Gap for lineage:** every reverse traversal ("what does this book/note feed into?") is an ad-hoc O(all-sub-theories √ó evidence) scan ‚Äî e.g. the book-delete cascade at `js/views.js:5473-5485` walks every sub-theory's evidence array to find references. There is no stored reverse index. A lineage feature that wants "this value ‚Üí these arcs ‚Üí these sources" would need either a reverse index or to accept full scans.

### 4. Value-tagging on notes / sub-theories / books ‚Äî DOES NOT EXIST

There is no value/lineage tag on any content record. `grep -rn "valueTag\|valueId\|valueIds\|lineage\|derivedFrom\|sourceBookId" js/` returns zero field definitions (only the prose word "lineage" in About copy at `js/views.js:14279` and unrelated "provenance" comments about the reader-model summary). Notebook entries are created with a fixed shape ‚Äî `{id, userId, register, isPrivate, body, bookIds, arcIds, images, filed, createdAt, updatedAt}` (`js/views.js:1776-1788`, `:10169-10181`) ‚Äî with no tag/value/category slot. Sub-theories likewise (`createSubTheory` `js/state.js:1736-1754`). A value-load feature that wants "this note advances value X" has no field to write to today.

### 5. Backfill-chokepoint asymmetry ‚Äî arcs and themes are splat-only (readiness risk for any new edge field)

Books and sub-theories have idempotent field chokepoints (`ensureBookFields` `js/state.js:387`, `ensureSubTheoryFields` `js/state.js:626`) that the Firestore merge honors, so new schema fields backfill on cross-device sync. **Arcs and userThemes have NO such helper** (`grep "function ensureArcFields\|function ensureThemeFields\|function ensureEntryFields"` = 0 matches): the arc merge splats remote records verbatim (`js/integrations.js:145-149`) and the theme merge likewise (`js/integrations.js:234-238`); notebook entries get only three ad-hoc inline defaults on merge. Any lineage field added to arcs, themes, or entries in a future build will silently fail to backfill on a device syncing from an older client ‚Äî the exact class of bug the book/sub-theory chokepoints were built to prevent. This is captured as a MEDIUM ledger item because it is a standing latent gap, not yet triggered.

### 6. Export / clear coverage of the value-lineage substrate

`exportWorkspace` (`js/state.js:1500-1528`) emits `profile` (incl. `values`), `books` (incl. `category`/`tradition`/`rawCategories`), `arcs`, `subTheories`, `notebookEntries` ‚Äî but **omits `bookArtifacts` and `userThemes`**. `userThemes` (the "lenses" the portrait emblem counts at `js/views.js:13011-13012`) are thus unexportable, and `clearUserState` (`js/state.js:1530-1543`) does NOT reset `state.userThemes` ‚Äî so on account switch a prior user's lenses persist in memory until overwritten by the per-uid REPLACE merge. Both are MEDIUM consistency gaps in the lineage/value substrate.


---

## PASS 5 ‚Äî Synthesis

## Architecture map

Praxis 2.0 is a pure static site (Netlify) backed by Firebase/Firestore, written in strict ES3 vanilla JS (`var`/`function`, string concat, two-arg `.then`) with no build step and no libraries. The client is ~27,200 in-scope LOC across a fixed script load order; the proxy layer is five Netlify functions in front of billable upstreams; a service worker (CACHE_VERSION praxis-v3.150) precaches the app shell.

**Load order (index.html / sw.js precache):** `state` ‚Üí `integrations` ‚Üí `yumi-brain` ‚Üí `arcs` (dead 12-LOC stub) ‚Üí `arc-constellation` ‚Üí `tradition-forms-arc` ‚Üí `voice-input` ‚Üí `yumi-ui` ‚Üí `views` ‚Üí `app`, with `arc-constellation` and `tradition-forms-arc` loading before `views`. `spotlight`, `writing-canvas`, and `import-capture` also ship. By size the in-scope top three are `views.js` (14,526 LOC, ~53% of in-scope code), `state.js` (2,944), and `yumi-brain.js` (2,800); `integrations.js` (2,073) is the only ES3-parse-exempt-by-design file. `verify-engine.js` (dead tombstone) is loaded by nothing.

**State / storage / durability.** Top-level `state` (state.js:271-285) holds per-uid `users` (yumiMemory/registerDefaults/profile/readerModel), a shared `books` map indexed per-uid via `userBooks`, plus `notebookEntries`, `bookArtifacts`, `arcs`, `subTheories`, and `userThemes` (lenses); `notebooks` is vestigial. `ls()`/`sv()` are the only localStorage path in all of `js/`, bucketed per-uid by `stateKey()`. `saveState()` is one synchronous localStorage write (return value never checked) plus five fire-and-forget dirty-flag-gated Firestore writes; only books re-dirty on failure and carry a persisted `pendingBookSync` guard ‚Äî arcs/notebook/subTheories/themes have neither, so a failed cloud write is silently lost under REPLACE-on-auth. `migrate()` is a forward-only 1.0.0‚Üí1.26.0 chain (anchor default '1.9.3'); the Firestore merge in `onAuthStateChanged` never calls it and instead relies on `ensureBookFieldsAll`/`ensureSubTheoryFieldsAll` chokepoints ‚Äî but arcs and themes splat verbatim with no backfill helper, and notebook entries get only three ad-hoc inline defaults. IndexedDB stores photo blobs only.

**Proxy / PWA layer.** All 18 client‚Üíproxy fetch sites carry `X-PRAXIS-KEY` (`PRAXIS_CLIENT_KEY` literal in the bundle); third-party openlibrary.org calls correctly omit it. The five functions (claude/elevenlabs/google-books/transcribe/vision) gate inside `if(expectedKey)`, failing open if the env var is unset. The service worker precaches the shell and requires a manual CACHE_VERSION bump per JS change.

**Yumi gate + moves.** `gradeUtterance()` (yumi-brain.js:707, system at :549) is the frozen, fail-closed gate ‚Äî every path (empty/budget/parse/timeout) returns `{pass:false}`, memoized, daily-capped at 200, 12s timeout. `assembleContextData()` (:178) is the single context source (alias `getContextSnapshot`; consumed by chat-prose and the transparency view) ‚Äî but the `isPrivate` filter is re-implemented at six move/aggregation sites that bypass it. Moves: QUIET/DRAW-OUT/COMPLICATE (`generateMove`), NOTICE/NAME (`considerNotice`/`considerName`), plus arc-voice, the classify router, web-grounding, lens generation, and profile refresh. Eight calls are timeout-wrapped; three are not (`sendMessage` chat, `summarizeAndRoll`, `generateLenses`) and nothing uses an AbortController.

**Dual-ground design system.** `:root` in theme.css is the bright-page base; an override block (theme.css:336-361) keyed on `[data-ground="dark"], .app-nav, .yumi-bloom, .yumi-panel, .spotlight-panel` remaps 18 ink/surface/border/gold tokens to the dark study palette. `views.js:369-371` sets `data-ground="dark"` on home/books/arcs/arc/account, bright elsewhere. Single-valued-both-grounds tokens (river, question, marginalia/teal, journal, danger, wordmark, gold-soft) are NOT remapped ‚Äî the root cause of most contrast failures, since several land sub-AA on one ground.

**Structure list**
- `js/state.js` ‚Äî state shape, ls/sv, saveState, migrate, ensureBookFields chokepoint
- `js/integrations.js` ‚Äî Firebase auth, REPLACE-on-auth merge, proxy fetches, volumeToBook
- `js/yumi-brain.js` ‚Äî frozen gate, assembleContextData, the move set, web-grounding
- `js/yumi-ui.js` ‚Äî chat panel, Bloom FAB, mic wiring
- `js/views.js` ‚Äî all route renderers (~53% of in-scope code), book/arc/notebook/account
- `js/arc-constellation.js` + `tradition-forms-arc.js` ‚Äî sub-theory constellation renderer
- `js/writing-canvas.js` ‚Äî shared composing core (adopted only at marginalia)
- `js/import-capture.js` + `js/voice-input.js` + `js/spotlight.js` ‚Äî import/dictation, search
- `netlify/functions/*-proxy.js` ‚Äî five gated upstream proxies
- `assets/theme.css` (tokens, dual-ground) + `assets/components.css` (~2,900 var() uses)
- `sw.js` ‚Äî APP_SHELL precache, CACHE_VERSION praxis-v3.150

### Severity-tagged issue ledger (130 findings)

_Status column: confirmed / adjusted (file:line corrected during verification) / unverified (verifier did not return a verdict)._

| # | Sev | Finding | Location | Why it matters | Verify |
|---|-----|---------|----------|----------------|--------|
| 1 | CRITICAL | Cloud-save failure is silent and never retried for arcs/notebook/subTheories/themes ‚Äî REPLACE-on-auth then loses the write cross-device | `js/state.js:2196-2279` | Each of the four non-book Firestore blocks clears its dirty flag at the top of the block (arcsDirty=false :2197, notebookDirty=false :2218, subTheoriesDirty=false :2239, themesDirty=false :2260) and the failure branch only console.warns ‚Äî it never re-dirties and there is no pending-guard. A transient cloud-write failure is therefore permanent: localStorage holds the write, but on the next device the REPLACE-on-auth merge (integrations.js:133-149 deletes all local arcs for the uid then splats stale remote) clobbers it. Books alone are protected by re-dirty-on-failure (:2191) plus the persisted pendingBookSync set (:785-831); arcs/notebook/subTheories/themes have neither, so user-authored arcs, journal/marginalia entries, published sub-theories, and manual themes can vanish silently on device switch. | confirmed |
| 2 | CRITICAL | Book Artifacts are localStorage-only ‚Äî never synced to Firestore, lost cross-device/on clear | `js/views.js:10242` | The Artifact is the ceremonial write-once 'yours' object (card copy promises it is permanent, views.js:6229), but it never reaches the cloud. New device, fresh install, or localStorage clear silently loses every Artifact. This is silent data loss on a core path. | confirmed |
| 3 | HIGH | saveState() return value (localStorage success bool) is never checked by any of its 52 callers ‚Äî local write failure is fully silent | `js/state.js:2152` | saveState returns `ok` from `sv(stateKey(), state)`, but sv() swallows any exception and returns false (:266-268). No caller inspects the result, so on a quota-exceeded or private-mode browser every save is a silent no-op: no user-visible error, no console output, and the in-memory state diverges from the 'durable' store the file's own comment (:2148) guarantees. | confirmed |
| 4 | HIGH | All 5 proxies fail OPEN when PRAXIS_CLIENT_KEY is unset, exposing billable upstreams | `netlify/functions/claude-proxy.js:22-35` | The gate runs only inside `if (expectedKey) {...}`. When the env var is unset or empty, the key check is skipped entirely and any anonymous POST is forwarded to Anthropic / ElevenLabs / Google Books on the project's billable keys. A missing or mistyped env var silently turns the entire AI backend into an open relay. Memory notes the SEC header was 'INERT until Preston sets the Netlify env var' ‚Äî i.e. there has already been a live window where the gate was off. The same pattern is duplicated verbatim in all five functions (elevenlabs-proxy.js:40-53, google-books-proxy.js:22-35, transcribe-proxy.js:47-60, vision-proxy.js:22-35). | confirmed |
| 5 | HIGH | Primary chat path (sendMessage) has no fetch timeout ‚Äî a hung proxy permanently locks the chat | `js/yumi-brain.js:770` | sendMessage's fetch is a raw .then() chain with no _yumiWithTimeout and no AbortController. yumi-ui.js sets yumi_request_in_flight=true and disables the send button before the call (yumi-ui.js:1230-1231) and clears them only in .finally (yumi-ui.js:1254). If the connection hangs without ever settling (no response, no RST), the promise never resolves/rejects, .finally never fires, and the chat stays locked (button disabled, typing indicator stuck) until a full page reload ‚Äî a hang without recovery. | confirmed |
| 6 | HIGH | --wordmark/--gold-soft text on bright ground is ~1.5:1 (effectively invisible) | `assets/components.css:4207, 4288, 4781` | --wordmark resolves to --gold-soft #e7c46a on BOTH grounds (theme.css:307; not in the dark override). On the bright notebook page (.notebook-entry-add-to-arc is a 12px text link) it lands on --page #f8f1e1 / --surface #fcf6e8, a 1.49-1.56:1 ratio - far below AA 4.5:1 and below even the 3:1 UI floor. The link text is essentially unreadable pale-gold on cream, an accessibility blocker on a core capture affordance. | confirmed |
| 7 | HIGH | --river / --question-color text on the dark ground is 1.98:1 | `assets/components.css:425-426` | --river #3a5a8a and --question-color (=--river) are never remapped for the dark ground (absent from theme.css:336-361). Where they are used as label/link text on a dark study surface - e.g. .ground-chip.web inside the dark Yumi panel - the ratio against --surface-d #3e2814 is 1.98:1, below both the 4.5:1 normal-text and 3:1 UI thresholds. | confirmed |
| 8 | HIGH | --meta (--ink-3/--ink-4) meta text fails AA on every bright surface (3.41-3.56:1) | `assets/components.css:2685-2691` | On the bright ground --ink-3 and --ink-4 resolve to --meta #9a7e4e (theme.css:62-63), giving 3.41:1 on --page and 3.56:1 on --surface - below AA 4.5:1 for normal text. These are the dominant meta/byline colors: --ink-3 is used as color 223 times and --ink-4 66 times. Concrete small-text uses on bright pages include .book-detail-meta (11px) and .notebook-entry-ts (10px), so dates/bylines across book-detail, notebook, subtheory, and about are sub-AA. | confirmed |
| 9 | HIGH | --ink-3 / --ink-4 meta text fails WCAG AA contrast on the light ground (3.56:1) | `assets/theme.css:33,62,63 (contrast confirmed); counts: var(--ink-3)=225 total / 45 as color, var(--ink-4)=83 total / 12 as color (not 'color:var(--ink-3)'=223)` | --ink-3 and --ink-4 both resolve to --meta (#9a7e4e); on --surface/--surface-2 (#fcf6e8) that is 3.56:1, below the 4.5:1 AA bar for normal text. Used 223+83 times, heavily on 10.5-11.5px mono eyebrows/labels/meta lines, so a large share of secondary text app-wide is sub-AA for low-vision readers. | adjusted |
| 10 | HIGH | Mobile hamburger is the only nav affordance and is a ~28px tap target | `assets/components.css:3871` | At <=759 the full nav collapses to .app-nav-hamburger, shown display:block (5416) with font-size:28px, padding:0, line-height:1 and no min-height/width. The single primary mobile navigation control is ~28x28px, well under the 44px touch minimum, making it hard to hit reliably on phones. | confirmed |
| 11 | HIGH | Reader-portrait master toggle advertises role=button + tabindex=0 but is keyboard-dead | `js/views.js:13836, 13857` | The rmtoggle is rendered <div data-act="rmtoggle" tabindex="0" role="button"> so AT and keyboard users expect Enter/Space to activate it, but its only handler (13857) listens for 'click'. There is no keydown bridge, so a keyboard user can focus it and press Enter/Space to no effect, with no other path to toggle Yumi-noticing. | confirmed |
| 12 | HIGH | Arcs grid never collapses to 1-up on mobile ‚Äî mobile override selectors target ids as classes (canon F broken) | `assets/components.css:5730-5733` | The Arcs page renders 3 columns at phone widths instead of the canon-F 1-up. The base rule .arcs-grid{repeat(3,1fr)} (components.css:1821) is the only rule on the live container and has no max-width:759 override; the override that exists uses class selectors .arcs-yours/.arcs-examples that match nothing because JS assigns those names as ids. | confirmed |
| 13 | HIGH | Constellation text fails AA contrast on the dark #arc route (light inks on the SVG's own bright goldenrod ground) | `js/arc-constellation.js:853, 862, 1106-1107, 1129, 1268` | On #arc (data-ground="dark") theme.css remaps --ink-2/3/4 to #c2a87f and --ink to #f0e3c8 (light), but the sub-theory SVG paints an opaque BRIGHT goldenrod ground (url(#tfa-stage), #fbf2da->#d8bd80, tradition-forms-arc.js:73-77) and .arc-detail-web-view::before is blanked (components.css:5998). | 14 | HIGH | renderArcDetail List branch reads arc.bookIds/entryIds.length unguarded ‚Äî crashes on a backfill-less arc | `js/views.js:9924, 9934` | A single arc record lacking entryIds (Firestore splat-merge has no ensureArcFields backfill ‚Äî no such helper exists ‚Äî and migrate() is not run on the merge path) throws TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'length') and aborts the entire arc-detail render. Same defensive-gap class as the v3.143 account white-screen. The same function guards every other read of these arrays. | confirmed |

| 16 | HIGH | Chat reply fetch has no timeout and no AbortController ‚Äî UI hangs without recovery if the proxy stalls | `js/yumi-brain.js:770` | The user-facing chat path (sendMessage) is the only interactive proxy call not wrapped in _yumiWithTimeout. If the proxy accepts the connection but never responds, the promise chain in runChat never settles: the typing indicator stays forever, yumi_request_in_flight stays true, and the Send button stays disabled with no path back. The audit's covenant requires graceful failure, not a hang. | confirmed |
| 17 | HIGH | segmentDoc has no client-side timeout/abort ‚Äî bulk import + dictation "sorting" beat can hang with no visible escape; dictated note is lost on hang | `js/import-capture.js:141 (fetch), 498 + 1262 (renderProcessing w/o onType)` | segmentDoc's fetch to claude-proxy has no AbortController and no setTimeout (contrast the dictation transport's 20s hard cap at :1054-1062). renderProcessing only renders a close button + 'type instead' escape when onType is passed (:483,:488); the bulk-import call (:498) and the post-transcription processDictation call (:1262) both pass NO onType, so the panel shows only 'Reading your notes‚Ä¶' / 'sorting your note‚Ä¶' with no in-panel exit. | 22 | MEDIUM | clearUserState() omits state.userThemes ‚Äî stale manual themes persist across an in-memory user wipe | `js/state.js:1530-1543 (resets 11 maps/pointers + SCHEMA_VERSION, not 10; userThemes declared :284, omitted)` | clearUserState resets 10 maps/pointers but does not clear state.userThemes, which is a real top-level map in the default state object (:284). | 23 | MEDIUM | exportWorkspace() (account 'Export to JSON' backup) silently omits bookArtifacts and userThemes | `js/state.js:1500-1528` | The user-facing Export to JSON button (views.js:14143-14162) calls exportWorkspace, whose returned object includes profile/books/arcs/subTheories/notebookEntries but NOT bookArtifacts (the user's per-book syntheses) or userThemes (manual themes). | 24 | MEDIUM | Gate shared-secret is hardcoded in the public client bundle | `js/integrations.js:18` | PRAXIS_CLIENT_KEY = '25a123...bcdd5' is a literal in client JS shipped to every browser and trivially readable in DevTools. It therefore provides no authentication ‚Äî anyone can copy it and call the proxies. It is only anti-casual-scraping friction. This is by design (the SEC gate), but the value is a fixed 64-hex string with no rotation/expiry, so once leaked the only remediation is a coordinated env-var + bundle redeploy. Worth recording as known debt, not a true access control. | confirmed |
| 25 | MEDIUM | Main Yumi chat proxy call has no client-side timeout ‚Äî can hang indefinitely | `js/yumi-brain.js:770-805` | The user-facing sendMessage chat fetch to claude-proxy has no AbortController and is NOT wrapped in the project's own _yumiWithTimeout helper (which exists and is used for the gate, grader, web-grounding, and move calls). If the upstream stalls, the chat 'thinking' state never resolves and the user gets a hang with no recovery path. The summarizeAndRoll path (yumi-brain.js:92) and the TTS path (integrations.js:2055) and Google Books (integrations.js:1447) and vision scan fetch (views.js:5873) are likewise unbounded; the scan only has a categorize-side ccWatchdog (views.js:3169), not on the vision fetch. | confirmed |
| 26 | MEDIUM | isPrivate privacy predicate re-implemented at 7 sites instead of routing through assembleContextData | `js/yumi-brain.js:218 (canonical) + 5 re-implementations at :266,:386,:1690,:1901,:2251 ‚Äî 6 predicate sites total, not 7` | assembleContextData is the single context source only for chat-prose + the transparency view. The move generators (considerMove, _visibleEntriesForScan/scan, gatherArcContext, getAggregateCounts, artifacts) each carry their own copy of the isPrivate filter. The privacy contract holds today but a future change to what counts as private must be made in all 7 places or a private note leaks into an LLM prompt ‚Äî exactly the failure principle #5 exists to prevent. | adjusted |
| 27 | MEDIUM | Firestore arc and theme merges splat remote docs with no field backfill, breaking the documented merge-boundary pattern | `js/integrations.js:145` | The code's own comment at :191-199 establishes ensureXFieldsAll at the merge boundary as 'the standing pattern for every future schema field' because the wholesale remote copy bypasses migrate(). Books (:601) and sub-theories (:197) follow it; arcs (:145-149) and themes (:234-238) splat the remote map with zero backfill, and no ensureArcFields/ensureThemeFields helper exists. No present-day crash, but the next per-record schema field added to arcs or themes will reintroduce the exact data-shape drift this pattern prevents. | confirmed |
| 28 | MEDIUM | Notebook-entry Firestore merge backfills only 3 fields ad-hoc; no ensureNotebookEntryFields helper | `js/integrations.js:282` | The notebook merge inlines defaults for exactly three fields ‚Äî filed (:282), journal isPrivate (:298), images (:309) ‚Äî instead of calling a centralized ensure-fields helper (none exists). | 30 | MEDIUM | yumi-brain.js and yumi-ui.js cannot be ES3 parse-validated (use .catch/.finally) | `js/yumi-brain.js:26,123 (.catch) + js/yumi-ui.js:1249 (.catch),1254 (.finally); combined LOC 4,728 (yumi-brain 2800 + yumi-ui 1928), not 5,531` | These two files (5,531 combined LOC, including the frozen Yumi gate and the command router) use promise .catch()/.finally(), which the ES3 cscript harness cannot parse, so they have no static parse gate and a syntax regression in them only surfaces on the live deploy. This is documented/accepted in CLAUDE.md, but it means the project's most logic-dense files ship without the parse safety net every other core file has. | adjusted |
